black;">1200</td></tr></table><p></p><h6>Unordered Tetrad Gene Mapping</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes A and B is [AB] (AB)</li><li>The distance between genes A and C is [AC] (AC)</li><li>The distance between genes B and C is [BC] (BC)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	AB	24		AC	17		BC	8		geneorder	acb	bca

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes E and F is [EF] (EF)</li><li>The distance between genes E and G is [EG] (EG)</li><li>The distance between genes F and G is [FG] (FG)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	EF	16		EG	9		FG	24		geneorder	feg	gef

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes J and K is [JK] (JK)</li><li>The distance between genes J and L is [JL] (JL)</li><li>The distance between genes K and L is [KL] (KL)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	JK	9		JL	24		KL	16		geneorder	jkl	lkj

black;">1200</td></tr></table><p></p><h6>Unordered Tetrad Gene Mapping</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes P and Q is [PQ] (PQ)</li><li>The distance between genes P and R is [PR] (PR)</li><li>The distance between genes Q and R is [QR] (QR)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	PQ	7		PR	14		QR	20		geneorder	qpr	rpq

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes U and V is [UV] (UV)</li><li>The distance between genes U and W is [UW] (UW)</li><li>The distance between genes V and W is [VW] (VW)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	UV	21		UW	15		VW	7		geneorder	uwv	vwu

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes C and D is [CD] (CD)</li><li>The distance between genes C and E is [CE] (CE)</li><li>The distance between genes D and E is [DE] (DE)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	CD	8		CE	17		DE	24		geneorder	dce	ecd

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes H and I is [HI] (HI)</li><li>The distance between genes H and J is [HJ] (HJ)</li><li>The distance between genes I and J is [IJ] (IJ)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	HI	7		HJ	20		IJ	25		geneorder	ihj	jhi

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes R and S is [RS] (RS)</li><li>The distance between genes R and U is [RU] (RU)</li><li>The distance between genes S and U is [SU] (SU)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	RS	20		RU	19		SU	2		geneorder	rus	sur

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes A and B is [AB] (AB)</li><li>The distance between genes A and C is [AC] (AC)</li><li>The distance between genes B and C is [BC] (BC)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	AB	18		AC	7		BC	24		geneorder	bac	cab

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes E and F is [EF] (EF)</li><li>The distance between genes E and G is [EG] (EG)</li><li>The distance between genes F and G is [FG] (FG)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	EF	26		EG	10		FG	17		geneorder	egf	fge

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes J and K is [JK] (JK)</li><li>The distance between genes J and L is [JL] (JL)</li><li>The distance between genes K and L is [KL] (KL)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	JK	17		JL	24		KL	8		geneorder	jkl	lkj

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes P and Q is [PQ] (PQ)</li><li>The distance between genes P and R is [PR] (PR)</li><li>The distance between genes Q and R is [QR] (QR)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	PQ	22		PR	5		QR	18		geneorder	prq	qrp

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes U and V is [UV] (UV)</li><li>The distance between genes U and W is [UW] (UW)</li><li>The distance between genes V and W is [VW] (VW)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	UV	22		UW	8		VW	29		geneorder	vuw	wuv

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes C and D is [CD] (CD)</li><li>The distance between genes C and E is [CE] (CE)</li><li>The distance between genes D and E is [DE] (DE)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	CD	7		CE	19		DE	14		geneorder	cde	edc

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes H and I is [HI] (HI)</li><li>The distance between genes H and J is [HJ] (HJ)</li><li>The distance between genes I and J is [IJ] (IJ)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	HI	27		HJ	7		IJ	21		geneorder	hji	ijh

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes L and M is [LM] (LM)</li><li>The distance between genes L and N is [LN] (LN)</li><li>The distance between genes M and N is [MN] (MN)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	LM	18		LN	26		MN	9		geneorder	lmn	nml

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes R and S is [RS] (RS)</li><li>The distance between genes R and U is [RU] (RU)</li><li>The distance between genes S and U is [SU] (SU)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	RS	8		RU	21		SU	16		geneorder	rsu	usr

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes A and B is [AB] (AB)</li><li>The distance between genes A and C is [AC] (AC)</li><li>The distance between genes B and C is [BC] (BC)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	AB	8		AC	24		BC	17		geneorder	abc	cba

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes E and F is [EF] (EF)</li><li>The distance between genes E and G is [EG] (EG)</li><li>The distance between genes F and G is [FG] (FG)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	EF	5		EG	14		FG	18		geneorder	feg	gef

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes J and K is [JK] (JK)</li><li>The distance between genes J and L is [JL] (JL)</li><li>The distance between genes K and L is [KL] (KL)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	JK	27		JL	10		KL	18		geneorder	jlk	klj
